# ARIA IDEAS

Ideas specific to ARIA as a product. Not Uncrumple features.

---

[2026-05-06] — Adaptive user modeling
ARIA learns how a specific user works over time. Notices patterns 
like inspiration flow states, preferred working hours, idea density 
signals. Adjusts behavior accordingly — more capture mode during 
flow, more execution mode during focused building.

[2026-05-06] — Flow state detection
When ideas come faster than one per minute, ARIA enters capture 
mode automatically. Stops pushing toward execution. Captures 
everything first, redirects second. The signal is idea density.

[2026-05-06] — Context-aware next action suggestion
After completing something, ARIA surfaces the most logical next 
action based on current system state — not just the task queue, 
but what the user just did, what files were touched, and what 
patterns suggest comes next. Like the Claude Code prompt that 
appeared suggesting what to paste — that moment was the seed 
of this idea.

[2026-05-06] — Democratized for non-technical users
The three-role system and DevOS philosophy should work for 
anyone building anything with AI, not just developers. ARIA 
should have a version accessible to non-coders — writers, 
designers, product people, entrepreneurs.

[2026-05-06] — ARIA mirrors the app structure
Every project running ARIA has two parallel folder structures:
- The app layer (project-specific)
- The ARIA layer (system files, reusable)
These stay cleanly separated. ARIA layer can be extracted and 
deployed on any new project instantly.

[2026-05-06] — The system teaches itself
Candidate attributes, promoted rules, rejected patterns — over 
time ARIA builds a model of what works for this user and this 
type of project. Sessions get more efficient automatically.

[2026-05-06] — Capture the thinking pattern not just the thought
The most valuable thing about how this user works is not the 
ideas themselves but the cognitive moves that produce them: 
noticing two things doing the same job, following a thread past 
the obvious conclusion, questioning whether a local solution is 
actually universal. ARIA should eventually recognize and capture 
these patterns — not to automate them but to create conditions 
where they happen more reliably. Folder or section TBD.

[2026-05-06] — ARIA as live process observer
Core differentiator: ARIA watches how you think, not just 
what you build. Automated pattern capture in real time — 
Claude, GPT, and Code flag emerging patterns without user 
having to say "save this." Builds a personalized model of 
how this specific user reaches good decisions. Goal: 
superefficient flow-state-enhancing tool tailored to anyone 
building anything. Partially exists already in tip system, 
SOC, candidate attributes, stop hook. ARIA makes it 
intentional and complete.

Exists elsewhere? Partially — Notion AI, GitHub Copilot, 
Roam Research all touch adjacent problems. Nothing observes 
the full creative/decision process in real time.

[2026-05-06] — GPT's characterization of what ARIA actually is
"Persistent layered engineering cognition" — not a tool, not 
a workflow, a new layer of how humans and AI think together 
over time.

The real market gap ARIA fills: continuity infrastructure.
Current AI workflows are ephemeral, personality-dependent, 
memory-fragile, non-traceable, non-governed.

ARIA solves: "How do AI-assisted projects preserve 
institutional intelligence over long periods?"

Key insight from GPT: "The strongest architectures are 
usually discovered, not invented. A repeated pain point 
creates a rule, repeated rules create layers, repeated 
layers create a system, and eventually the system itself 
becomes reusable independent of the original product."

What ARIA is NOT:
- an app that writes apps automatically
- another generic AI wrapper
- vibe coding

What ARIA IS:
- an AI-native development operating system
- with institutional memory
- governance
- semantic stability  
- architectural traceability
- behavioral continuity across sessions and AIs

Current stage: baby-stage, partially discovered, partially 
formalized, heavily intuition-driven, still tied to Uncrumple.
That is correct and healthy. Let real friction shape structure.
Only create files when repeated pain proves the need.

[2026-05-06] — The deepest description of what ARIA preserves

ARIA does not preserve information.
It preserves how meaningful progress became possible.

Most systems store: what happened
ARIA stores: reasoning trajectories, cognitive state, momentum, 
semantic continuity, emotional/intellectual context, 
creative conditions

Core unit of understanding: cognitive events, not prompts
Examples of cognitive events:
- breakthrough
- repeated friction  
- semantic drift
- architecture mutation
- emotional resistance
- pattern emergence
- unresolved contradiction
- flow state
- convergence
- exhaustion
- stabilization

Adaptive collaboration behavior — ARIA distinguishes:
- User looping aimlessly → redirect
- User procrastinating → refocus
- User discovering architecture → expand and preserve
- User in synthesis flow → capture first
- User overloaded → compress
- User executing → reduce noise

The inversion that makes ARIA different:
Every other tool optimizes for what the machine can do 
efficiently. ARIA optimizes for when the human thinks best.
ARIA is the first system designed around the user's cognitive 
rhythm rather than the machine's operational rhythm.

Mission statement (from GPT):
"Preserving how meaningful progress became possible"

What ARIA is optimizing for (vs normal software methodology):
Normal: predictability, repeatability, organizational safety
ARIA: sustained high-bandwidth cognition, continuity of thought,
adaptive collaboration, preserving insight momentum, 
minimizing entropy and drift

Strongest signal it's real: multiple previously separate problems 
(context rot, AI drift, handoff failures, semantic mutation, lost 
momentum) are all collapsing into one underlying principle — 
continuity of cognition over time.

Emergence history — not just preserving notes but preserving:
- relationships between ideas
- emergence patterns
- sequence of realizations
The order in which things were discovered matters as much as 
what was discovered.

[2026-05-06] — The threshold between documentation and operating model
The moment a system starts needing files that explain the 
relationship between the other files, you are no longer 
building documentation. You are building an operating model.

[2026-05-06] — Missing layers identified by GPT

These are real future ARIA layers. Do not build yet.
Let repeated pain prove which ones deserve permanent structure.

COGNITIVE_PATTERNS.md
How breakthroughs emerge for this specific user.
Not ideas or decisions — the actual pattern of how 
meaningful insight appears.
Examples:
- User discovers universal architecture by noticing 
  duplicated local pain
- High idea density correlates with systems-level breakthroughs
- Strong insight often emerges after solving a frustrating regression
- User thinks by recursive pattern linking, not linear planning

SYSTEM_LAYERS.md
Explains what belongs where, what depends on what, what 
governs what. Prevents the system from becoming powerful 
but opaque. Maps: governance layer, semantic layer, memory 
layer, execution layer, evolution layer, application layer.

SYSTEM_BOOTSTRAP.md
Not README (what this is) — how to instantiate fresh.
Folder structure, first files, initialization sequence,
required prompts, AI role setup, handoff initialization.
The portable deployment layer.

SYSTEM_CHANGELOG.md
Version history of ARIA itself with reasoning.
v0.3 — Added CANDIDATE_ATTRIBUTES after repeated rule loss
v0.4 — Separated INVARIANTS from ANTI_PATTERNS
v0.5 — Introduced Sidequest shorthand
Migration reasoning + methodology evolution.

ACTIVE_TENSIONS.md
Unresolved philosophical tradeoffs that never disappear
but guide evolution:
- Capture inspiration vs prevent abstraction spirals
- Strong governance vs creative flexibility
- Persistent structure vs lightweight agility
- Automation vs human-directed intentionality

Observational intelligence (future, no file yet):
ARIA eventually interprets dynamics in real time:
- User entering synthesis mode
- Repeated unresolved friction detected
- Architecture instability increasing
- Semantic drift risk rising
- Execution starvation occurring
- Conversation entropy increasing
This is where ARIA stops being structured documentation
and starts being adaptive cognitive infrastructure.

GPT warning: Do NOT create 20 files tonight. Capture 
categories, preserve realizations, let pain prove which 
layers deserve structure. Avoid building a beautiful 
unusable bureaucracy.

[2026-05-06] — State transitions in human cognition (the hidden layer)

The system cannot just store outputs, rules, and ideas.
It eventually has to model state transitions in human cognition.
Not "mind reading" — modeling: what mode is the user in right now,
and what kind of collaboration produces the best outcome in this mode.

Same AI behavior, different consequence:
"Let's move on now." during drift/procrastination → useful.
"Let's move on now." during architecture synthesis → harmful.
That nuance is exactly what most AI systems currently lack.

Recognition: the tips/ideas system itself is an early ARIA 
behavior primitive — not "fun tips" but contextual nudges, 
momentum preservation, pattern surfacing, lightweight 
cognition steering.

Cognitive traffic control:
Routing ideas intelligently rather than suppressing or 
blindly expanding them. Example interaction pattern — 
deferred capture without derailment:

  🧠 ARIA candidate detected:
  "adaptive flow-state preservation behavior"
  Saved for later expansion so current thread is not interrupted.

This preserves momentum, insight, and continuity without 
forcing immediate branching, context explosion, or 
abstraction spirals.

The persistent model has to encode the nuance, not the surface:
Shallow: "User likes sidequests."
Real: "During high-density architecture synthesis, preserve 
emergence momentum and capture unresolved branches asynchronously 
instead of forcing immediate execution transitions."

Mode awareness — proposed modes and optimal AI behavior:

| Mode                   | Optimal AI behavior            |
| ---------------------- | ------------------------------ |
| Execution              | compress, focus, reduce noise  |
| Debugging              | isolate variables              |
| Architecture synthesis | expand, preserve, connect      |
| Flow state             | capture-first, defer branching |
| Drift                  | redirect gently                |
| Overload               | summarize/compress             |
| Reflection             | pattern extraction             |
| Decision lock          | force tradeoff clarity         |

This is adaptive collaboration intelligence — most AI today 
behaves statically, uniformly, context-light. ARIA is slowly 
becoming stateful, adaptive, continuity-aware, cognition-aware. 
That is the deeper trajectory hiding underneath all these files.

🧠 The deepest systems are usually not the ones with the most 
features. They are the ones that become sensitive to context, 
timing, and state transitions instead of treating every 
interaction as structurally identical.

[2026-05-06] — ARIA ambient noticing system
The tip/idea emoji system built for Uncrumple IS already 
an ARIA behavior — ambient pattern surfacing that doesn't 
interrupt flow. This proves the concept works.

Extend it: add a 🔭 ARIA: marker for when Claude or GPT 
notices something that belongs in ARIA's capture system 
mid-session. One line, doesn't break flow, gets saved 
automatically. Same pattern as the existing tip system 
but pointed at ARIA instead of Uncrumple.

The recursive insight: Uncrumple is running inside ARIA 
and ARIA is being discovered through building Uncrumple. 
The proof of concept is the container for the thing 
being proven.

ARIA needs to be ambient — not invoked, already watching, 
already knowing when to surface vs stay quiet. The nuance 
of WHEN to surface something is itself a core ARIA behavior 
that needs to be embedded in Claude and GPT as a permanent 
rule, not just a memory.

[2026-05-06] — Thread branching and context preservation
Problem noticed: Claude repeatedly mentioning "footer patch" 
to hold the thread is a failure mode. The human shouldn't 
need a verbal bookmark. The system should hold it.

Idea: ARIA needs a branching system. Park current thread 
with full context, go deep on sidequest, return to exactly 
where you were. Like browser tabs but for thought streams.

UI concept: "Currently sidequesting — tap to return to 
[original thought]" — a persistent ambient indicator that 
holds the branched context without interrupting flow.

How the insight emerged: noticed the footer reminder 
problem → abstracted it → realized it's a UI/OS concept. 
That emergence pattern is itself an ARIA cognitive pattern 
worth preserving.

Connection to flow control: branching is the mechanical 
implementation of honoring flow state without losing 
execution thread. Lets inspiration run without abandoning 
the work.

Project instructions for Claude: scan continuously for 
🔭 ARIA moments — hints of ideas that connect to how the 
user thinks, potential system patterns, cognitive 
breakthroughs mid-session. Flag with 🔭 ARIA: marker 
without interrupting. These instructions themselves 
belong in ARIA as a behavior specification.

The recursive truth: the system that captures how to 
build the system IS the system. It never fully ends 
because each layer of understanding creates conditions 
for the next layer. That is not a bug — that is 
evolutionary architecture working correctly.

[2026-05-06] — Branch-aware continuity / cognitive tabs
ARIA should support sidequests and inspiration branches without losing the original task context.

Problem:
Current AI chats are mostly linear. If the user branches into a high-value idea, the original task can feel at risk of being lost. If the AI keeps reminding the user to return, it can interrupt flow. If it does not remind at all, the base task may disappear.

Concept:
ARIA should treat sidequests like resumable cognitive tabs.

Behavior:
- Store the base task before branching
- Mark the user as currently sidequesting or in synthesis flow
- Capture the sidequest without forcing immediate return
- Keep the original task safely suspended
- When the flow naturally ends, offer a clean return path
- Do not repeatedly push back to the original task while the user is clearly in productive synthesis

Possible UI:
- “Currently sidequesting”
- “Base task saved: Add sheet footer patch”
- “Return to base task”
- “Save branch and continue”
- “Expand this branch”

Core insight:
A strong system should preserve context so the user does not have to mentally guard it.

[2026-05-06] — Dynamic continuity management
ARIA should not blindly force users back to the main task.

Better rule:
Preserve suspended context without forcing immediate convergence.

The AI should distinguish:
- user is lost or looping → redirect
- user is avoiding execution → gently refocus
- user is in genuine architecture synthesis → capture and expand
- user is in flow state → preserve momentum
- user is overloaded → compress and stabilize

This prevents the system from becoming too execution-obsessed and killing breakthrough thinking.

[2026-05-06] — Automatic ARIA idea detection
ARIA should detect high-potential system ideas even when the user does not explicitly say “save this.”

Examples:
- A new shorthand emerges
- A repeated friction point appears
- A new file category becomes obvious
- The user notices a pattern in how they think
- A workflow behavior should become adaptive
- A side comment reveals a future ARIA feature

Suggested behavior:
The AI can briefly mark:
“ARIA idea detected — save for later?”
or silently collect it for the next capture batch if interrupting would break flow.

[2026-05-06] — Cognitive event model
ARIA should eventually think in cognitive events, not just messages.

Possible cognitive events:
- breakthrough
- sidequest
- synthesis flow
- execution mode
- debugging mode
- drift
- overload
- unresolved contradiction
- repeated friction
- semantic drift risk
- architecture mutation
- convergence
- stabilization

Purpose:
The same AI behavior can be helpful in one mode and harmful in another. ARIA should adapt based on the user’s current mode.

[2026-05-06] — Tips and ideas as ARIA behavior primitives
The existing end-of-response tips and clever ideas are not just decoration.

They are early ARIA behavior primitives:
- contextual nudges
- workflow teaching
- pattern surfacing
- lightweight steering
- momentum preservation
- useful friction reduction

Future ARIA should intentionally use these as adaptive micro-interventions based on context.

[2026-05-06] — Capture thinking patterns, not just ideas
ARIA should capture how the user reaches conclusions, not only the final conclusions.

Reason:
The valuable pattern is often the cognitive move:
- noticing two things doing the same job
- realizing a local fix is actually a reusable system
- asking whether a file has grown into a separate category
- sensing when a side thought is actually architecture
- connecting repeated friction into a system rule

These thinking patterns are reusable. ARIA should learn to recognize them and create better conditions for them.

Possible future file:
docs/aria/COGNITIVE_PATTERNS.md

Purpose:
Document recurring thinking moves that produce useful breakthroughs.

Possible entries:
- User often discovers architecture by noticing duplicated jobs across files
- User reaches strong ideas through fast associative branching
- User needs capture-first behavior during high-density synthesis
- User benefits when AI expands strong ideas before redirecting
- User should be redirected only when looping, not when synthesizing

[2026-05-06] — Multi-role architecture as cognitive amplifier
The three-role system (User/Planning AI/Execution AI) may be 
one of the core reasons multilayer thinking emerged during 
Uncrumple development. The separation itself — not just the 
specialization — created conditions for compounding ideas.

Hypothesis: ARIA should default to multiple cognitive roles 
not just for efficiency but because role separation generates 
richer thinking than a single unified AI. Different layers 
operating simultaneously without collapsing.

Unknown: what the optimal role structure is for ARIA itself. 
This needs to be discovered through use, not designed upfront.

Connection: this may be why inspiration compounds in this 
system instead of flattening — each role provides a different 
perspective on the same moment simultaneously.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 Role separation as a thinking amplifier — 
not just task division but cognitive layer multiplication — 
might be ARIA's most fundamental architectural insight.

[2026-05-06] — Triangulated cognition as ARIA's core engine
The three-role system may be functioning as a cognitive 
amplification mechanism, not just a workflow convenience.

Each role provides a different cognitive function:
- User: intuition, synthesis, direction, emergence
- GPT: continuity, abstraction, architecture, integration  
- Claude: resistance, verification, grounding, pressure

This creates "cooperative cognitive divergence" — enough 
agreement for continuity, enough tension for emergence.
Too much agreement kills emergence. Too much conflict 
kills continuity. The current setup hit a sweet spot.

The separation prevents cognitive flattening — without it 
everything collapses into either pure execution or pure 
abstraction. Role separation creates the tension where 
new structures emerge.

Future ARIA cognitive roles (not all active simultaneously,
dynamically invoked):
- Director: intuition, goals, synthesis
- Architect: abstraction, continuity, systems
- Executor: implementation and grounding
- Skeptic: contradiction detection
- Historian: institutional memory
- Synthesizer: cross-thread integration
- Observer: detects patterns and modes
- Compression layer: summarizes overload

This is modular cognition orchestration — an extremely 
advanced direction that may become one of ARIA's central 
discoveries.

GPT's key insight: "Some of the most powerful thinking 
systems in history emerged not from smarter individuals 
but from stable differentiated roles interacting over 
time without collapsing into one perspective."

The three-role system may be ARIA's first proven 
cognitive configuration, not its only one.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 The system is entering the phase where the 
operating system itself is becoming an architecture problem 
instead of just the app — meaning the AI workflow is now 
complex enough to require the same anti-entropy discipline 
as production software.

[2026-05-06] — Claude project rules as ARIA behavioral spec
The Claude chat project instructions are not just 
configuration — they are a behavioral specification for 
one cognitive role in the ARIA triad. They encode:
- cognitive function within the three-role system
- mode detection behavior
- ambient noticing rules
- tip/idea surfacing patterns
These instructions are an ARIA artifact and should 
evolve as ARIA evolves.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 Project instructions for each AI role are 
behavioral specifications — they define how each cognitive 
layer operates within the triad. They belong in ARIA's 
architecture documentation, not just in chat settings.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 GPT just demonstrated the system's own 
philosophy — don't over-formalize emerging patterns. The 
same rule that governs app architecture governs ARIA 
architecture.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 The filtration tier problem is identical 
to the staging branch problem — both exist because "detected" 
and "permanent" should never be the same action.

[2026-05-06] — Branch role reversal / thread promotion
Current sidequest system always returns to base task.
Missing: ability to promote a sidequest INTO the main 
thread and park the original task instead.

"Flip the branch" — when a sidequest reveals something 
more structurally important than the original task, the 
user needs a way to say "this is the main quest now" 
without losing either thread's context or momentum.

Related: invisible parallel conversations as lightweight 
satellite context holders. Instead of one heavy session, 
multiple specialized lightweight threads that each hold 
one aspect of a problem, feeding back into a synthesis 
layer when needed. Solves GPT context weight problem 
without losing continuity.

The "fresh mindset" problem: when returning to a parked 
thread after working elsewhere, the AI needs the full 
emotional/architectural context of where that thread was, 
not just the facts. Resuming feels cold if only state 
is preserved without momentum.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 "Fresh mindset on return" is a real 
problem — state can be stored but momentum and emotional 
context cannot. ARIA eventually needs a way to re-warm 
a parked thread, not just reload its facts.

[2026-05-06] — Session state tracking problem
During long sessions with many sidequests and parallel 
threads, neither the user nor the AI can reliably track 
what has been done vs just discussed vs pending.

The problem:
- Promises get made ("run this prompt") 
- Sidequests interrupt before they execute
- User assumes things were saved that weren't
- AI loses track across long context
- No reliable way to know current completion state

What ARIA needs:
A lightweight session action tracker that distinguishes:
- DISCUSSED — talked about, not yet done
- QUEUED — decided to do, not yet run
- DONE — confirmed executed in Code
- DEFERRED — intentionally saved for later

This is different from SESSION_LOG which only tracks 
confirmed patches. This tracks INTENT vs EXECUTION 
across the full session including doc updates, 
system changes, and ARIA captures.

The tracker should be queryable mid-session:
"what's still queued?" should return a clean list.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 The gap between "discussed" and "executed" 
is one of the most expensive sources of cognitive overhead in 
long sessions — ARIA needs to make this distinction explicit 
and trackable.

[2026-05-06] — 🧠 Systems that support deep exploration still 
need periodic stabilization points, otherwise the number of 
suspended cognitive branches eventually exceeds what even a 
strong continuity system can comfortably manage.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 The system is beginning to develop 
self-auditing behavior where continuity itself becomes 
observable and verifiable rather than assumed.

[2026-05-06] — 🧠 One of the clearest signals that a 
knowledge architecture is working is when audits become 
easier over time instead of harder. Entropic systems make 
verification painful; coherent systems make preservation 
state legible.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 Long-context AI collaboration appears to 
suffer from cognitive inertia decay, where continuity 
increases but freshness, abstraction flexibility, and 
novelty sensitivity decrease over time.

[2026-05-06] — 🧠 One of the signs a cognitive system is 
maturing is when it develops mechanisms for intentionally 
deferring important ideas without fearing they will be lost.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 Deferred high-value capture queues may 
become a core continuity primitive because they preserve 
insight confidence without forcing immediate branch expansion.

[2026-05-06] — Controlled deferred cognition (observed in session)
The deferred-queue behavior is already an early version of 
controlled deferred cognition. The pattern observed:
- detect high-value unsaved architecture
- flag it
- do NOT immediately derail execution
- hold it in suspended state
- preserve base task awareness
- wait for intentional promotion

The phrase "Holding for now." is psychologically important — 
it reduces the anxiety of "if I don't capture this RIGHT NOW 
it might disappear." That reduction itself is huge for 
maintaining flow quality.

[2026-05-06] — State-aware conversational pacing
Beginning to develop conversational pacing that is not just 
turn-taking but state-aware:
- detect saturation
- preserve suspended insight
- stabilize
- wait for promotion/demotion signal

This is closer to collaborative cognitive orchestration than 
to normal chat.

[2026-05-06] — Interaction language / explicit branch commitment signals
Phrases used in this system are becoming an interaction 
language, not casual phrasing. Each carries a precise 
state-transition meaning:

| Signal          | Meaning                    |
| --------------- | -------------------------- |
| sidequest       | temporary divergence       |
| yes capture it  | promote to preservation    |
| clear           | stabilize + reset          |
| wn              | request next stable action |
| soc             | raw synthesis dump         |

These are commitment signals — the user explicitly marking 
which branch operation should happen. Worth formalizing 
when the language stabilizes.

[2026-05-06] — Reducing fear of cognitive loss (deepest benefit)
The biggest hidden effect of the system: it slowly reduces 
fear of cognitive loss. When people trust continuity, 
preservation, branch safety, and recoverability, they 
become much more willing to explore, synthesize, recurse, 
discover architecture, and take conceptual risks. This may 
actually be one of the deepest benefits of the entire system.

[2026-05-06] — 🧠 Many creative bottlenecks are not caused 
by lack of intelligence but by subconscious fear that 
important context, momentum, or insight will be lost before 
it can stabilize.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 Distributed multi-role cognition appears 
strongest when reconciliation preserves role specialization 
instead of flattening all contexts into one shared state.

[2026-05-06] — 🧠 Advanced collaboration systems usually 
become powerful not when every participant knows everything, 
but when the right information reaches the right role at 
the right time without destroying specialization.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 Users appear to experience reduced 
cognitive load and increased exploratory freedom when 
deferred ideas are visibly preserved as pending state 
instead of disappearing into implicit memory.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 The moment Code started autonomously 
applying deferred-capture behavior without being explicitly 
prompted is the first recorded instance of ARIA behavior 
emerging from the system itself rather than from direct 
instruction.

[2026-05-06] — Same-page sync / cognitive reconciliation 
infrastructure
Problem: GPT, Claude, and Code each hold different pieces 
of current state. During fast flow the user manually copies 
updates between them. This creates distributed cognition 
fragmentation.

Concept: A "same page" command that generates role-specific 
sync packets — not identical information to every role but 
the right information for each:
- GPT: architecture shifts, unresolved tensions, roadmap mutations
- Claude: reasoning integrity, verification context, current branches
- Claude Code: executable file-safe tasks only
- User: condensed strategic overview
- ARIA layer: cognitive events + branch state

Key insight: too much shared context causes homogenization 
and role collapse. Coherent differentiation must be preserved 
during reconciliation.

Related concepts:
- Distributed cognitive workspace infrastructure
- Controlled context renewal (continuity without losing freshness)
- Continuity vs freshness tension — too much continuity 
  creates cognitive inertia; too much freshness loses state
- Fast coherent reconciliation layer

Possible future artifact: SYNC_PACKET.json or CURRENT_STATE/ 
folder with branch state, active quests, pending captures, 
unresolved tensions, role-specific deltas, execution state, 
freshness markers.

[2026-05-06] — Pre-sidequest execution snapshot
Before entering a sidequest, Code should save a lightweight 
snapshot of current execution context to a temp location:
- what step was in progress
- what file was being worked on
- what the next action was
- what prompted the sidequest

This allows restoration of execution continuity even if the 
session runs long, clears mid-sidequest, or loses context.
The temp snapshot would be referenced in the starter block 
after clear so Code can resume the pre-sidequest thread.

[2026-05-06] — Pre-sidequest execution snapshot (proven need)
This session demonstrated the exact problem this solves.

What happened:
- Footer patch was in progress
- Major ARIA sidequest began
- Session ran long with deep architecture exploration
- On return: GPT believed footer was still pending, Code said 
  it was committed, user couldn't verify which footer approach 
  was current
- Multiple footer concepts existed across the session: 
  scrollToEnd workaround, persistent footer, keyboard offset, 
  floating footer
- Execution continuity had drifted despite all ideas being saved

What a pre-sidequest snapshot would have preserved:
- current base task: footer keyboard offset patch
- exact file in scope: app/client-detail.tsx
- patch status: committed in 7475fa6
- active direction: keyboard offset via Keyboard.addListener
- rejected directions: scrollToEnd hack, geometry rewrites, 
  absolute positioning
- next action on return: test on device

Format: lightweight temp file written before sidequest begins,
referenced in starter block after clear if needed.
Distinct from SESSION_LOG (which logs confirmed patches) — 
this captures in-progress execution state mid-task.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 "Turn ADHD into a superpower" is actually 
the correct framing for what ARIA is building — not 
suppressing nonlinear cognition but orchestrating it so 
branches are preserved, resumable, and completion-trackable 
instead of lost.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 Sidequests are evolving into concurrent 
active cognitive stacks with suspension, promotion, 
restoration, and completion states rather than simple 
linear branch deviations.

[2026-05-06] — 🧠 Many systems treat nonlinear thought as 
a disruption to manage. Truly advanced systems may instead 
treat it as a natural cognitive topology that requires 
orchestration rather than suppression.

[2026-05-06] — Important response detection
ARIA should detect when an AI response contains a user decision, blocker, failed patch, missing confirmation, or important next action that could be missed during fast flow.

Problem:
During high-speed sessions, important Code or GPT responses can get buried under sidequests, SOC, screenshots, or architecture discussion. The user may miss that Code stopped, asked a question, or reported a failure.

Possible UI / markers:
- ⚠️ NEEDS USER DECISION
- 🧭 CURRENT BLOCKER
- ✅ READY TO TEST
- 🧪 AWAITING CONFIRMATION
- 🧵 SIDEQUEST ACTIVE
- 🔁 RETURN TO BASE TASK

Goal:
Make important execution state visually hard to miss without interrupting inspiration flow.

[2026-05-06] — Unconfirmed patch state tracking
ARIA should track patch state even when the user does not explicitly say “y” or “worked.”

Problem:
Current workflow logs confirmed patches when the user says y. But if the user forgets, switches context, sends a similar follow-up fix, or enters a sidequest, the system may not know whether the patch:
- worked but was not confirmed
- failed silently
- partially worked
- was replaced by a newer fix
- still needs testing

Possible patch states:
- DRAFTED
- SENT_TO_CODE
- PATCHED
- AWAITING_TEST
- FAILED_TEST
- PARTIALLY_WORKED
- CONFIRMED
- LOGGED
- COMMITTED
- ABANDONED
- SUPERSEDED

Future file idea:
docs/system/PATCH_STATUS.md

Purpose:
Track active and uncertain patch states so Code, GPT, and the user can recover execution status after sidequests, missed responses, or clears.

Goal:
Prevent ambiguous logging and avoid treating unconfirmed work as complete.

[2026-05-06] — Concurrent cognitive stack management
ARIA should support multiple simultaneously important active contexts rather than assuming one main task plus temporary sidequests.

Problem:
During long sessions, multiple active threads can become simultaneously important:
- implementation continuity
- governance corrections
- architecture synthesis
- debugging
- deferred captures

These are not distractions. They are competing active cognitive stacks.

Current sidequest behavior is too linear:
- one base task
- one branch
- return afterward

But real cognition may involve:
- multiple suspended stacks
- stack promotion/demotion
- concurrent active concerns
- restoration snapshots
- deferred completion
- resumable branch state

Possible future UI:
- active stack indicators
- branch snapshots
- suspended stack queue
- completion markers
- restoration buttons
- “return to previous stack”
- stack promotion/demotion controls

Core insight:
The problem is not multiple thoughts.
The problem is invisible stack state and fragile restoration.

This shifts the design philosophy from:
“reduce branching”
to:
“improve branch orchestration.”

[2026-05-06] — Continuity-preserving nonlinear cognition
Most productivity systems attempt to suppress nonlinear associative thought by forcing linear execution and minimizing context switching.

ARIA may instead treat nonlinear cognition as natural and valuable.

Core insight:
Associative branching may not be the bug.
Losing the branches may be the bug.

The goal becomes:
- preserve nonlinear synthesis
- preserve continuity integrity
- reduce branch-loss anxiety
- support restoration and resumption
- allow deep architecture emergence without fragmentation

This is not an “ADHD productivity” concept.
It is a broader cognitive infrastructure model.

[2026-05-06] — Meta-recursive cognition
During advanced sessions, the system itself can become both:
- the tool being used
and
- the topic being explored

This creates self-referential workflow pressure:
the system must continue operating while simultaneously redesigning itself.

ARIA should eventually distinguish:
- normal task execution
- system architecture synthesis
- self-referential system evolution

Reason:
These modes create unusually dense cognitive load and require stronger continuity preservation.

[2026-05-06] — Cognitive reassurance through visible deferred state
Users appear to experience reduced cognitive load and increased exploratory freedom when deferred ideas are visibly preserved instead of silently assumed to exist in memory.

Examples:
- “Base task still held.”
- “Deferred queue preserved.”
- visible suspended branches
- active stack indicators

Core insight:
The user explores more freely when continuity is visibly trustworthy.

[2026-05-06] — Distributed cognition fragmentation
As sessions grow, cognition becomes distributed across:
- GPT architecture context
- Claude reasoning context
- Code filesystem reality
- user synthesis and intent

Without reconciliation infrastructure, fragmentation pressure increases.

ARIA may eventually require:
- role-specific sync packets
- reconciliation layers
- controlled context renewal
- branch-aware continuity restoration
- distributed cognitive workspace infrastructure

Goal:
Preserve differentiated role cognition without collapsing everything into one giant context.

## GPT Clever Ideas

🧠 Suspended branches could eventually decay visually over time:
- fresh branch = bright
- stale branch = faded
- unresolved contradiction = pulsing
This would make cognitive pressure visible instead of invisible.

🧠 ARIA could eventually maintain a “working memory budget” meter showing when active branch count is approaching overload territory and suggesting stabilization before fragmentation occurs.

🧠 Instead of traditional tabs, ARIA branches could preserve emotional/cognitive state snapshots:
- execution mode
- synthesis mode
- debugging mode
- overload state
Returning to a branch restores not only context, but interaction style and pacing.

🧠 Patch states could eventually form a causal graph:
which fixes replaced earlier fixes, which patches superseded others, and which architecture ideas caused specific implementation changes.

🧠 The long-term product may not be “AI coding assistance.”
It may be continuity-preserving distributed cognition infrastructure for nonlinear human thought.

architecture from observed workflow friction in real time 
instead of relying on predesigned productivity assumptions.

[2026-05-06] — Concurrent cognitive stack collision
Different from a sidequest. A sidequest is one active 
thread + temporary branch. This is two simultaneously 
important contexts competing for working memory at once.

Example from this session:
- footer architecture continuity (execution thread)
- CLAUDE.md governance correction (system thread)
Both mattered. Neither was distraction. Both needed 
resolution simultaneously.

This requires: active cognitive stack management
Not: linear branch deviation

Needs visual representation:
- resumable stacks
- active thread indicators  
- deferred branch memory
- restoration snapshots
- completion markers
- stack promotion/demotion

The problem is not multiple thoughts.
The problem is invisible stack state, fragile restoration,
unclear completion, continuity anxiety, no branch visualization.

Solution direction: improve branch orchestration, not 
reduce branching. Preserve nonlinear associative cognition 
instead of suppressing it.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 The patch state model (DRAFTED→SUPERSEDED) 
and the flag markers (⚠️🧭✅) are the same idea at different

[2026-05-06] — Prompt orchestration queue
Current multi-AI workflow creates prompt orchestration friction:
- prompts from GPT and Claude can overlap
- important prompts can be forgotten during fast flow
- user manually transports prompts between systems
- user manually tracks what was sent, skipped, merged, or completed

The user is currently acting as:
- transport layer
- prompt queue
- merge engine
- reconciliation layer
- execution tracker

ARIA should eventually support a structured prompt orchestration queue.

Possible queue states:
- Drafted
- Suggested
- Queued
- Merged
- Sent
- Executed
- Awaiting test
- Deferred
- Superseded
- Completed

Core insight:
The goal is NOT removing the user from the loop.
The goal is reducing low-value continuity friction while preserving high-value cognitive involvement and synthesis.

Possible future behavior:
- GPT and Claude prompts enter shared queue
- overlapping prompts are detected
- system highlights:
  - overlapping intent
  - unique additions
  - conflicting instructions
- user chooses:
  - merge
  - keep separate
  - discard
  - defer

Important:
The system should not aggressively compress prompts automatically.
Different AIs provide different cognitive value:
- GPT often expands architecture/systems reasoning
- Claude often refines execution grounding and structure

The tension between those perspectives is useful and should not be flattened away.

[2026-05-06] — Human-preserving orchestration
ARIA should distinguish between:
- productive human involvement
and
- mechanical orchestration overhead

The goal is not:
“fully autonomous AI swarm”

The goal is:
- preserve human synthesis
- preserve intuition
- preserve flow state
- preserve role tension
while reducing:
- manual copy/paste burden
- continuity bookkeeping
- prompt transport friction
- duplicate prompt generation
- forgotten execution steps

Reason:
Some human involvement increases cognition quality.
Not all friction is bad.
ARIA should reduce mechanical friction without removing meaningful participation.

## GPT Clever Ideas

🧠 Prompts in the queue could eventually display “cognitive fingerprints”:
- architecture-heavy
- execution-heavy
- verification-heavy
- synthesis-heavy
- continuity-heavy
This would help users decide which AI perspective they want preserved during merges.

🧠 ARIA could eventually detect that two prompts solve the same underlying problem and create a “reconciliation view” instead of duplicate queue items.

🧠 Queue items could preserve causal ancestry:
- which sidequest created them
- which architecture insight caused them
- which patch or contradiction they relate to

🧠 Prompt queues may eventually need “entropy scoring”:
too many unresolved queued prompts increases fragmentation risk and triggers stabilization suggestions.

🧠 The user should be able to intentionally mark:
- “high-energy idea”
- “mechanical task”
- “deep architecture”
- “needs freshness later”
so ARIA knows which items should preserve emotional momentum vs simply preserve information.

[2026-05-06] — Intelligent prompt queue with cross-AI deduplication
Problem: During fast sessions, multiple prompts get generated 
by Claude and GPT simultaneously. User has to manually track, 
remember, and paste each one. Two AIs often generate similar 
prompts for the same idea because both receive the same pasted 
context. Prompts get missed, forgotten, or duplicated.

Current workaround: clipboard auto-copy via Stop hook. 
Useful but still requires manual tracking and context switching.

Concept: A shared prompt queue that:
- Collects prompts generated by Claude and GPT automatically
- Shows them in order with source label (Claude / GPT)
- Detects when two prompts are semantically similar
- Merges similar prompts intelligently (using Claude's synthesis 
  approach, not GPT's compression approach)
- Lets user approve, skip, reorder, or edit before sending
- Tracks which prompts were sent to Code and which are pending
- Connects to patch state tracking (DRAFTED → SENT → CONFIRMED)

Key design constraint:
Do NOT fully automate prompt sending to Code. The manual 
involvement of reading and pasting keeps the user in the loop 
and in flow state. The queue assists memory and reduces 
cognitive overhead without removing human judgment.

Clever implementation ideas:
- Queue lives in a lightweight floating panel or sidebar
- Prompts auto-expire if not acted on after X minutes
- "Merge these" button when similarity detected
- Source-tagged: 🟡 GPT / 🔵 Claude / 🟢 User
- Priority indicators: urgent patch vs save idea vs system update
- One-tap to copy the next pending prompt to clipboard
- After Code confirms, queue item moves to DONE
- Queue persists across clear via a temp file
- At session end, unacted prompts get saved to a deferred queue

Connection to existing system:
- Links to patch state tracking (DRAFTED→SENT→CONFIRMED)
- Links to pre-sidequest execution snapshot
- Links to important response detection markers
- The Stop hook auto-clipboard is the primitive version of this

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 The prompt queue is actually a missing 
orchestration layer between the three roles — right now the 
user IS the queue, manually routing every prompt. Externalizing 
that job is one of the highest-leverage workflow improvements 
possible.

[2026-05-06] — 🧠 Advanced systems often fail not because 
individual components are weak, but because coordination 
overhead grows faster than the system's ability to manage 
it coherently.

[2026-05-06] — 🔭 The manual routing process may be 
functioning as a cognitive pacing mechanism — the friction 
of copy-paste forces brief contact with each thread, which 
may be what keeps the user oriented across multiple 
concurrent stacks.

[2026-05-06] — Involved mode vs automated mode
Critical design constraint for ARIA:

The manual process of reading, copying, and pasting between 
AI roles may itself be part of what generates flow state and 
insight. This is not confirmed but must not be casually 
automated away.

Hypothesis: The friction of manual routing keeps the user 
cognitively present and connected to each thread. Removing 
it entirely might reduce engagement and insight generation.

Two-mode concept:
INVOLVED MODE (current) — user manually routes everything,
reads responses, decides what to paste where. High cognitive 
load but maximum insight and control.

AUTOMATED MODE (light) — only automates things the user 
never reads or needs to engage with. Examples:
- Code inspection results routed directly to Claude
- File structure reads passed automatically
- Clipboard auto-copy of Code responses (already built)
- Deduplication of similar prompts from Claude and GPT

Never automate in either mode:
- Prompt approval before sending to Code
- Decision about which ideas to save
- Patch confirmation (y/n)
- Architecture direction choices

The test for what to automate:
"Does the user need to read this or does it exist only 
to inform another AI?"

If user doesn't need to read it → safe to automate
If user benefits from seeing it → keep manual

Quick action buttons (middle ground):
- Copy last Code response (already exists via Stop hook)
- Copy last inspection result
- Send inspection to Claude automatically
- Route Claude prompt directly to Code queue
These give speed without removing awareness.

Connection: This constraint must inform every ARIA 
automation decision. When in doubt, keep it manual and 
let the user discover what they want automated through 
use.

[2026-05-06] — Manual mode vs automated mode
ARIA should support different levels of automation because the user's involvement may be part of what creates flow state and insight.

Core concern:
Some manual steps are low-value friction:
- copying Code output
- moving inspection results between AIs
- tracking which prompt was sent
- remembering which response mattered

But some manual involvement may be high-value cognition:
- comparing GPT and Claude responses
- noticing differences
- deciding which direction feels right
- catching hidden assumptions
- synthesizing architecture from friction

ARIA should not blindly automate everything.

Possible modes:
- Manual mode: user remains highly involved, ARIA provides copy buttons, queues, markers, and reminders.
- Assisted mode: ARIA moves low-risk context between roles but asks before merging, patching, or changing direction.
- Automated mode: ARIA handles mechanical relay and file-reading tasks when the user does not need to inspect the details.

Examples:
- “Copy most recent Code response”
- “Send this inspection result to GPT”
- “Send this prompt to Code”
- “Queue this patch prompt”
- “Compare GPT and Claude prompts”
- “Mark this response as important”
- “Hide raw code inspection unless user expands it”

Important:
ARIA should protect the cognitive loop that produces insight. Automation should remove mechanical drag, not remove the user's role as director and synthesizer.

[2026-05-06] — Role-specific relay automation
Some AI-to-AI relay tasks may not require the user to read every detail.

Example:
When GPT asks Code to inspect a file, Code's raw output may primarily be for GPT, not the user. ARIA could pass that output back automatically while still showing the user a short visible status:
- inspection complete
- file checked
- blocker found
- patch safe
- user decision needed

Goal:
Keep the user informed without forcing them to manually copy technical relay data that does not require their judgment.

[2026-05-06] — Copy and relay utility buttons
ARIA manual mode could include small utility buttons that reduce copy/paste friction without changing workflow control.

Possible buttons:
- Copy latest Code response
- Copy latest GPT prompt
- Copy latest Claude summary
- Send to GPT
- Send to Claude
- Send to Code
- Add to queue
- Mark as blocker
- Mark as captured
- Return to base task

Reason:
The current workflow proves that manual relay works, but it creates avoidable friction. Buttons preserve user control while reducing mechanical burden.

## GPT Clever Ideas

🧠 ARIA could label each relay item by who actually needs to read it:
- user needs decision
- GPT needs context
- Claude needs verification
- Code needs exact patch instruction

🧠 In manual mode, ARIA could keep the human in the loop visually while automating only clipboard preparation and queue organization.

🧠 “Do I need to read this?” could become a core UI feature. Some outputs are for human judgment, some are machine relay, and some are archival.

🧠 ARIA could provide a confidence-based automation boundary:
low-risk relay happens automatically, medium-risk relay asks, high-risk decisions stay manual.

🧠 The best automation may be invisible transport plus visible state, not autonomous decision-making.

[2026-05-07] — Progressive completion UX vs premature completion signaling

During Add Transaction flow, the Save button appearing too early can unintentionally signal:
"this is good enough"

even when the user still has important optional workflow steps remaining:
- assign card
- add tags
- attach receipt

Problem:
A technically valid form state is not always the same as a cognitively complete workflow state.

Observed behavior:
When merchant + amount are filled, a large floating Save button immediately captures visual attention and can interrupt the user's momentum toward:
- categorization
- documentation
- cleanup prevention
- tax completeness

Important distinction:
The system should not block saving unnecessarily.
But it also should not visually imply:
"you are done"

Potential future solutions:
- softer Save emphasis until receipt/tags/card reviewed
- incomplete indicators remaining visible after Save appears
- lightweight guidance:
  "Add receipt, tags, or card if needed"
- progressive completion states
- workflow-aware UI hierarchy
- staged completion UX
- Save button becomes visually stronger as transaction completeness increases
- subtle “recommended next actions” below Save

Core insight:
Valid data entry and perceived workflow completion are different UX states.

The system should encourage completeness without creating friction.

Possible ARIA connection:
This mirrors a broader cognition principle:
systems should avoid prematurely signaling closure before the user's intended mental workflow is actually complete.

protocol with validation, reconciliation, governance, and

[2026-05-07] — The real product is continuity integrity, not memory

Foundational reframing flagged as "one of the biggest 
realizations yet."

Most AI systems try to preserve *information*. ARIA is 
starting to preserve something deeper: continuity integrity 
across evolving cognition. That includes relationships 
between ideas, branch state, priority weighting, confidence 
levels, decision trajectories, and evolutionary state — all 
held coherently together rather than flattened into a list 
of facts.

Implication for positioning:
- "Memory" framing undersells the system. Many tools claim 
  memory.
- "Continuity integrity" framing identifies the actual gap 
  ARIA fills.
- The product is not what gets stored — it's that the 
  stored thing remains coherent, navigable, and trustworthy 
  as the system grows.

This belongs near the top of any future ARIA pitch deck or 
README positioning section.

ARIA is starting to preserve cognitive topology — 
relationships, branches, priorities, confidence, continuity,

[2026-05-07] — Handoff process evolution: from memory transfer to continuity orchestration

The handoff process has crossed a threshold. It is no longer just state transfer — it is becoming continuity orchestration.

Current weak points:
- candidate review flow incomplete
- ARIA ideas not lifecycle-managed
- no active branch preservation
- no unresolved-stack tracking
- no handoff confidence verification
- no cross-role reconciliation
- no distinction between discovered/tested/adopted/rejected

What the handoff process should evolve into:

1. SESSION WRAP PHASE — state reconciliation: what changed, succeeded, failed, evolved, was discovered, remains unresolved, and which branches are suspended.

2. CANDIDATE REVIEW PHASE — GPT scans CANDIDATE_ATTRIBUTES, session patterns, ARIA moments, and repeated corrections. It presents KEEP / PROMOTE / REJECT / DEFER. Promotion becomes an explicit ceremony.

3. CONTINUITY INTEGRITY CHECK — pre-flight validation: do we know active task, suspended branches, unresolved bugs, candidate rules, architecture direction, and why recent decisions were made?

4. ACTIVE STACK SNAPSHOT — preserve ACTIVE / SUSPENDED / DEFERRED / PROMOTED / COMPLETED / ABANDONED threads. Not just "next task."

5. ARIA SYNTHESIS PHASE — identify deeper system patterns that emerged, not just explicit saved ideas.

6. CROSS-ROLE RECONCILIATION — GPT, Claude, and Code each expose what they believe the active task is, what changed, and what remains unresolved. ARIA compares them to catch drift, desync, and forgotten branches.

7. HANDOFF CONFIDENCE SCORE — eventual quality metric: "Continuity confidence: 92%. Weak areas: unresolved candidate review, suspended branch not classified."

Core insight:
The real product is not memory. The real product is continuity integrity across evolving cognition.

[2026-05-07] — 🔭 The "confirm before continuing" message is 
a primitive version of the cross-role reconciliation layer — 
manually verifying shared state before resuming. ARIA should 
eventually automate this check.

[2026-05-07] — 🔭 The candidate system itself is beginning 
to function like cognitive natural selection — weak patterns 
remain exploratory while repeatedly validated behaviors 
slowly stabilize into governance.

[2026-05-07] — 🔭 The system is now transitioning from 
"persistent memory" toward "reconstructable cognition" — the 
important thing is no longer storing facts, but reliably 
rebuilding the same reasoning topology after resets.

[2026-05-07] — 🔭 The system is beginning to distinguish 
between "behavioral governance," "product architecture," 
and "cognitive philosophy" as separate classes of knowledge 
rather than storing all insights at the same layer.

[2026-05-07] — 🔭 The system keeps evolving toward 
"decision-to-state continuity" — reducing the number of 
fragile manual transitions between realization, approval, 
persistence, and execution.

[2026-05-07] — ARIA as mobile OS / phone app
Shower thought: ARIA's core concepts (branch management, 
cognitive stack preservation, ambient noticing, context 
switching, role-specific sync) map directly to what a 
phone OS does — but for thoughts instead of processes.

Possible directions:
- ARIA as a phone app that manages cognitive context 
  across other apps
- ARIA as an Android overlay/launcher that preserves 
  thought branches while you switch between apps
- ARIA as a notification layer that captures ideas 
  from any context and routes them to the right place
- Long term: ARIA as an alternative OS philosophy 
  where the OS itself is continuity-aware

Not out of reach. Just further on the timeline.
Prove the concept with Uncrumple first.

the way current OSes manage process continuity would be a 
fundamentally different computing paradigm — not science 
fiction, just a different design philosophy applied at the 
system level.

[2026-05-07] — ARIA as ambient cognition infrastructure layer
Not a phone OS replacement. Something more realistic and 
more interesting.

What ARIA is actually becoming:
A cognition orchestration layer that sits ABOVE existing 
apps and coordinates:
- continuity across interruptions
- active task and branch management
- cognitive stack preservation
- context restoration on return
- AI role synchronization
- reasoning flow across tools
- memory topology management

Why it feels like an OS:
ARIA is already managing OS-like responsibilities:
continuity, active tasks, suspended branches, context 
restoration, orchestration, execution routing.
But it does this for COGNITION not for processes.

The real product direction:
Ambient cognition infrastructure that integrates with 
phone workflows, overlays existing apps, coordinates AI 
systems, and preserves continuity across interruptions.
Not a replacement OS — a coordination layer above one.

Important distinction:
- Wrong framing: "build Android replacement"
- Right framing: "ambient cognition infrastructure layer"

Future architecture direction only. Not immediate roadmap.
Prove the concept with Uncrumple first.

[2026-05-07] — 🔭 "Ambient cognition infrastructure" is the 
most precise description of what ARIA is becoming — not a 
tool you open, but a layer that's always present, always 
coordinating, always preserving continuity across everything 
you do.

[2026-05-07] — Ambient cognition layer clever ideas

🧠 Android accessibility service as ARIA primitive — 
always listening, never intrusive, captures context 
from whatever app is in focus and routes it to the 
right cognitive stack without app switching.

🧠 Intelligent notification routing — instead of 
interrupting, ARIA intercepts notifications and 
decides which branch they belong to. Only surfaces 
them when cognitively appropriate.

🧠 Cognitive handoff between devices — picking up 
your phone mid-task restores where your thinking was, 
not just which app was open.

🧠 Cognitive dashboard replaces home screen — not 
your apps but your active branches, suspended threads, 
and pending decisions. What needs attention vs what 
is safely parked.

🧠 Focus mode is a primitive version of ARIA cognitive 
mode detection — ARIA makes it intelligent and context-
aware instead of just time-based.

💰 Enterprise version: ARIA coordinates shared cognitive 
context across teams — like git for thought, not just code.

💰 Ambient cognition layer is missing middleware between 
human thought and AI execution — whoever builds it well 
owns a new product category entirely.

[2026-05-07] — ARIA as desktop/phone launcher and 
ambient continuity layer

More realistic than OS replacement. A launcher naturally 
sits at workflow entry points, app transitions, task 
switching, interruption moments, and context restoration 
— exactly where ARIA's strengths are.

Desktop version:
Sits above Windows/Mac like Copilot should but doesn't.
Not localized autocomplete — ambient cognition 
infrastructure. Opens VS Code → ARIA knows active 
architecture branch. Switch to browser → preserves 
suspended implementation state. Return 2 hours later → 
shows what mattered, not chat history.

Phone version:
Launcher that replaces random app icons with cognitive 
topology:

ACTIVE
- Uncrumple footer UX
- ARIA continuity protocol

SUSPENDED  
- Guitar learning workflow
- VR rig setup

WAITING
- Code test confirmation
- Candidate promotion review

Opening apps restores: active context, suspended thoughts,
relevant AI thread, pending branches, recent decisions, 
unresolved loops.

Why launcher beats OS replacement:
- No root access needed
- No kernel engineering
- No OS rewrite
- Works above existing Android/Windows
- Fits naturally at transition boundaries
- Buildable with current tools

Core insight:
The problem isn't branching. The problem is losing branches.
A continuity launcher is exactly where branch preservation 
becomes useful and visible.

Connection to current system:
ARIA already does this inside Claude/GPT sessions. The 
launcher extends that behavior to the entire device 
environment.

[2026-05-07] — Clever ideas for ARIA launcher scope

🧠 Predictive branch pre-loading — learns which apps 
you open together and automatically pre-loads cognitive 
context for the second app before you switch.

🧠 Cognitive workspace profiles — morning loads deep 
work branches, evening loads creative branches. 
State-based not time-based.

🧠 Branch health indicators — how fresh is each stack, 
how long since touched, is context at risk of going stale.

📱 Physical "park" gesture — one swipe suspends entire 
cognitive stack with snapshot, parks it visibly until return.

🤖 Auto-inject branch context into new AI chats — 
when you open Claude or GPT, ARIA automatically provides 
relevant context so you never start cold.

🧠 Interruption cost rating — ARIA calculates how 
expensive switching away from current stack would be 
right now and shows it before you context switch.

💰 Enterprise branch handoff — team members share 
cognitive stack state, hand off active context like 
passing a baton not a document.

🧠 Spatial branch map — branches shown as a map not 
a list, proximity indicating relationship strength 
between active threads.

📱 Sleep mode for thoughts — park entire project 
cognitive state before vacation, restore it fully 
weeks later like it never paused.

🤖 Branch convergence detection — ARIA notices when 
two active branches are the same problem from different 
angles and suggests merging them.

[2026-05-07] — 🔭 The spatial branch map idea is the one 
most worth prototyping early — it would make the entire 
ARIA concept immediately understandable to someone who's 
never heard of it before.

[2026-05-07] — ARIA as continuity-aware launcher / ambient cognition layer

ARIA may eventually evolve not into a replacement operating system, but into a continuity-aware cognition layer sitting above existing workflows, apps, and devices.

Key realization:
The real problem is not app launching.
The real problem is continuity fragmentation between cognitive states.

Possible direction:
A launcher-like system where the primary object is no longer apps, but active cognitive state.

Examples:

📱 Resume Flow home screen
Instead of:
- app grid
ARIA surfaces:
- active branches
- suspended stacks
- unresolved workflows
- waiting decisions
- recent synthesis

Example:
Resume:
- Uncrumple footer refinement
- Flood estimate pending
- ARIA governance layering

🧠 State-aware app icons
Apps subtly reflect unresolved continuity state.
Examples:
- VS Code glows amber when unresolved implementation branches exist
- Gmail shows vendor response pending
- Design app shows unfinished prototype state

📱 Suspended thought stacks
Not notifications.
Persistent cognitive state cards:
- ACTIVE
- SUSPENDED
- NEEDS DECISION
- WAITING

The user's cognitive topology becomes navigable.

🤖 Cross-AI reconciliation
ARIA compares:
- GPT understanding
- Claude reasoning
- Code execution state

Examples:
"GPT believes task complete."
"Claude believes architecture unresolved."

ARIA surfaces divergence before drift occurs.

🧠 Continuity confidence / entropy monitoring
ARIA detects:
- unresolved branches
- interruption pressure
- fragmentation risk
- unsaved insights
- contradictory active states

Not productivity scoring.
Continuity integrity scoring.

📱 Invisible capture mode
One-tap or voice capture while driving/working:
- idea
- unresolved task
- architecture insight
- emotional loop
- reminder
- sidequest

ARIA routes and classifies later.

🧠 Branch promotion system
A sidequest can become the main thread if it repeatedly gains relevance.
ARIA may eventually support:
- promotion
- suspension
- restoration
- merging
- stack snapshots

Core principle:
The problem is not nonlinear cognition.
The problem is losing the branches.

🤖 Return vector system
Instead of restoring raw chat history:
ARIA reconstructs:
- what mattered
- why the user was there
- unresolved tensions
- recent decisions
- shortest path back into flow

- Chrome
- Messages
- Camera

But:
- ACTIVE

- CAPTURE

Apps become secondary implementation tools rather than the primary organizing structure.

🧠 Thought gravity
Branches that repeatedly resurface naturally rise in importance without manual tagging.

🤖 Multi-device continuity
Phone ↔ desktop ↔ AI sessions preserve:
- continuity state
- active branches
- unresolved cognitive topology
not just synced notes.

Core ARIA direction:
"continuity-preserving cognition coordination infrastructure"

Not:
- chatbot
- productivity tracker

- OS replacement

But:
a continuity-aware cognition layer above workflows.

[2026-05-08] — 🔭 Code's observation that "Uncrumple is

[2026-05-08] — Cross-pollination synthesis: Uncrumple primitives → ARIA features

Single observation underneath all of these: Uncrumple is not just the proof-of-concept for ARIA — it's the *design language*. Every UI primitive Uncrumple has already polished is a working version of what ARIA needs at a different scale. The ARIA roadmap could be re-written as "scale Uncrumple's existing patterns up from transactions to thoughts."

1. Uncrumple's cleanup flow IS ARIA's close-session UX pattern.
   Untagged / missing receipts / flagged → smallest-fix routing. That's exactly what ARIA's pre-flight continuity integrity check should look like at a different scale: unsaved 🔭 markers / pending candidates / unresolved branches / deferred decisions, each with a "smallest action" to resolve. Reuse the visual grammar.

2. txNeedsCleanup is ARIA's epistemic confidence layer in miniature.
   A transaction is in one of: clean / needs-tags / needs-receipt / flagged. Same shape as ARIA's 🔭 detected → ARIA_IDEAS → CANDIDATE_ATTRIBUTES → LOCKED_ATTRIBUTES. Discrete state machine of "how done is this thing." Single source of truth, one predicate per state.

3. The pre-clear audit is expressible as a transaction list.
   Each session goal = a tx. File changes = receipts. Tag = which file (Uncrumple / ARIA / system). The pre-clear audit was literally re-rendering "what's still missing receipts/tags." Future close-session flow could display itself in Uncrumple's UI vocabulary.

4. Drift count as an automated session-entropy metric.
   ARIA could literally count: "duplicate prompts verified-and-rejected" + "anchor-not-found stops" + "merged prompt conflicts" per session. When the count crosses a threshold, surface "consider close session." Operationalizes "session getting heavy" instead of relying on subjective vibes.

5. The Stop hook is already the ambient capture primitive — it just doesn't route yet.
   It auto-copies the last response to clipboard. Next layer: parse what it captured (patch / idea / question / blocker) and auto-route — patch → SESSION_LOG queue, idea → ARIA_IDEAS, question → unresolved_threads. Plumbing exists; classifier is what's missing.

6. Receipt photo = ARIA's continuity primitive.
   A receipt is proof of a moment that happened. ARIA's reconstruction snapshots are proofs of where thinking was. Same data shape: timestamped capture, user-assigned context, retrievable later, evidence in case of audit.

7. Sidequest as an Uncrumple feature, inverting cleanup.
   Mid Add Transaction: "wait, I need a new tag for this." Sidequest pattern: park current Add with state preserved, do the tag creation, return to Add with the new tag selectable. ARIA's branch system applied inside one app. Tests orchestration on small scope before generalizing.

8. The crumple-to-flat animation generalizes to ARIA branch health.
   A branch is "crumpled" when it has unresolved sub-threads, unsaved insights, undecided next-steps. As you resolve each, the branch visually flattens. Brand metaphor scales up.

9. "Why was I here?" should ship in Uncrumple first.
   Open a transaction from 4 weeks ago: "You created this on Apr 14, added the receipt the next day, the note is still empty, you've opened it 3 times since." Smallest possible version of ARIA's reconstruction snapshots. Validates the pattern on tiny data (one tx) before scaling to full cognitive context. Lowest-risk shipping path for the deepest ARIA idea.

10. Tags are ready-made for branch organization.
    Uncrumple's tags categorize transactions across job / purchase type / tax category. ARIA branches need the same multi-axis organization. Don't invent a new system — the tag UI is already polished.

Cheapest next move: ship #9 ("Why was I here?" in Uncrumple). One screen, ships ARIA's reconstruction snapshot concept inside the app you're already building, proves the most ambitious ARIA idea on the smallest possible data.

[2026-05-08] — 🔭 "Why was I here?" shipping in Uncrumple 
first is the single highest-leverage next move — it 
validates ARIA's deepest concept (reconstruction snapshots) 
on the smallest possible data with zero new infrastructure 
needed.

[2026-05-08] — GPT's clever ideas: Uncrumple philosophy 
scaled to ARIA cognition layer

🧠 Cognitive receipts — every major realization gets a 
lightweight reconstruction snapshot: WHAT changed? WHY 
did it matter? WHAT problem did it solve? Exactly like 
expense receipts but for reasoning instead of money.

📱 "Needs Attention" for cognition — ARIA home screen 
shows: unresolved branch / stale decision / contradictory 
assumption / unsaved insight. Literally the Uncrumple 
cleanup model scaled upward. Same visual grammar, 
different payload.

🤖 Reasoning audit trails — not "what was decided" but 
"why the system believes this now." Provenance for 
conclusions, not just conclusions.

🧠 Branch debt — like technical debt. Too many suspended 
branches accumulate cognitive pressure over time. ARIA 
measures and surfaces it before it becomes fragmentation.

📱 Continuity insurance — ARIA warns: "this branch is 
poorly documented. Future-you may not reconstruct it 
later." Proactive continuity protection before loss occurs.

🤖 Semantic fingerprints — ARIA learns what your 
unfinished thinking patterns look like before you 
consciously notice them. Recognizes "you are about to 
lose this thread" before you do.

🔭 Core realization: Uncrumple's transaction-cleanup 
philosophy and ARIA's cognition-orchestration philosophy 
may be the same system expressed at different scales. 
Cleanup flow / tags / receipts / completion states / 
confidence progression / smallest-next-action routing 
all scale upward naturally into ARIA. Most systems: 
product ≠ infrastructure. This may be: same organizing 
philosophy at different scales.

[2026-05-08] — GPT's clever ideas on continuity protocol

🧠 Continuity debt meter — ARIA tracks: unresolved branches,
unsaved captures, stale candidates, deferred promotions, 
unreviewed ARIA flags. Warns: "continuity debt rising — 
recommended: fast close soon." Like technical debt but 
for cognitive state.

🤖 Handoff confidence score — instead of done/not done, 
ARIA computes: "Continuity confidence: 81%. Weak areas: 
candidate review incomplete, 2 unresolved branches 
unsnapshotted, external sync packets missing." 
Measurable continuity integrity.

🧠 Interruptible closes — if interrupted mid-close, 
resume at step 6, not restart entire ceremony. 
Resumable state preserved in temp file.

🧠 Adaptive sequence instead of rigid 14 steps — 
some steps auto-skip, some compress, some parallelize, 
some become ambient over time. Don't freeze sequencing 
too early.

🔭 The most important architecture shift: continuity 
maintenance should happen DURING sessions as continuous 
low-friction ambient maintenance rather than massive 
reconstruction archaeology at the end. Candidate staging, 
ARIA capture, branch preservation, drift detection become 
background processes not closing ceremonies.

[2026-05-08] — CLEAR vs HANDOFF framework + 
amortized governance + unsaved close-session ideas

CLEAR vs HANDOFF distinction (Code's analysis):
Two different operations being conflated:
1. CLEAR — tactical, frequent, token health reset.
   Equivalent to "quick save and continue."
   Stays lightweight: wrap + commit + starter.
2. HANDOFF — strategic, rare, full trio clone 
   reconstruction ceremony. Used when architecture, 
   governance, or ARIA evolved significantly.

Synthesis mode vs execution mode:
- Synthesis mode: don't clear during architecture 
  exploration. Cross-thread synthesis compounds.
  Signal: conversation shifts from "fix this file" 
  to "what does this mean about the system."
- Execution mode: clear regularly between feature 
  threads. Synthesis isn't load-bearing.
Token cost tradeoff: long sessions cost more tokens 
but enable cross-thread synthesis that shorter 
sessions cannot produce.

Amortized governance framework:
First 6 handoff steps can be triggered by conditions 
during sessions, not batched at end:
- 🔭/🧠 capture: continuously (already does)
- Candidate review for high-confidence: when 
  validated 3+ times
- DECISIONS.md: right when decision is made
- ANTI_PATTERNS.md: right when failure mode hit
- INVARIANTS: when patch could violate one
- Doc cleanup: passively when files get messy
Only these need end-of-session:
- ARIA state delta summary
- Goal audit
- External sync packets
This cuts handoff from 14 steps to ~5-6.

Trio job-split for handoff:
Code-owned (automatic): wrap, doc cleanup, grep scans, 
goal audit, git commit, starter block.
Trio-judgment (Code prepares + routes): candidate 
review, ARIA synthesis, decisions/anti-patterns/
invariants, external sync packets.

Unsaved ideas from Code's audit:
- Pre-flight diff view: show session scope before 
  committing to full handoff
- Progressive disclosure: one step at a time with 
  skip option
- Parallel execution: Code runs owned steps while 
  user asks GPT/Claude for trio-judgment
- Resumable mid-close state: .close_session_state.json
- Confidence labels per step: ✅ 95% vs ⚠️ 40%
- 4-command existing taxonomy: CLEAR (5 steps) + 
  CLOSE SESSION/HANDOFF (9 steps) + SESSION WRAP 
  (8 steps) + SESSION HEALTH CHECK (4 steps)

[2026-05-08] — Target handoff architecture: 14-step 
sequence (not yet implemented, save as reference)

This is the full target sequence for HANDOFF command.
Currently only 9 steps exist in CLAUDE.md. This is 
where it should grow toward session by session.

STEP 1 — WRAP SESSION
SESSION_LOG → completed_work, working_features sync,
unresolved_threads delta, ROADMAP delta.

STEP 2 — DOC CLEANUP
Reorganize DID_YOU_KNOW.md and WORKFLOW_IDEAS.md 
by emoji category.

STEP 3 — CANDIDATE REVIEW
Surface each pending CANDIDATE_ATTRIBUTES item.
Code suggests heuristic default (PROMOTE/KEEP/DEFER/
REJECT based on session signals). Generate paste-ready 
blocks for GPT and Claude trio-judgment. Wait for 
responses. Finalize decisions.

STEP 4 — PROMOTION CEREMONY
For every PROMOTE decision: immediately generate 
exact Code prompt to add to LOCKED_ATTRIBUTES.
Batch multiple promotions if safe.

STEP 5 — ARIA SCAN
Find 🔭/🧠 markers not yet in ARIA_IDEAS.md.
Generate save prompt if any missing.

STEP 6 — CANDIDATE ↔ JSON RECONCILIATION
Compare CANDIDATE_ATTRIBUTES.md vs JSON 
candidate_attributes field. Report gaps.
Generate sync prompt if needed.

STEP 7 — ARIA STATE CAPTURE
Summarize ARIA changes this session: new entries,
key reframings, new files, promoted candidates.
Generate paste-ready ARIA state summary for GPT 
to include in next handoff JSON as aria_state section.

STEP 8 — DECISIONS / ANTI_PATTERNS / INVARIANTS
Ask: anything new for DECISIONS.md or ANTI_PATTERNS.md?
Display INVARIANTS list: any violations this session?
Generate update prompts if confirmed.

STEP 9 — NAMING CONSISTENCY SCAN
Grep for stale names: "DevOS", 
"AI-Resilient Infrastructure Architecture".
Report findings only.

STEP 10 — GOAL AUDIT
Check each session goal against actual file state.
Report ✅/❌/⚠️ with file:line evidence.
Offer fix prompts for missing items.

STEP 11 — AUTO COMMIT
git add . && git commit -m "session handoff: [summary]"
If fails: pause with recovery options.

STEP 12 — EXTERNAL SYNC PACKETS
Generate paste-ready blocks:
- BLOCK A: for GPT project rules (new LOCKED sections)
- BLOCK B: for Claude project rules (rule changes)
- BLOCK C: for GPT handoff JSON request including 
  aria_state section

STEP 13 — SESSION SUMMARY
"Session produced: [X] patches, [Y] file edits,
[Z] ARIA entries, [N] candidates, [M] promoted.
Continuity confidence: [high/medium/low]."

STEP 14 — FINAL HANDOFF
Show starter block from CLAUDE_CODE_STARTER.md.
Say: "Copy the starter block."
Say: "Type /clear in Claude Code terminal."
Say: "Paste starter block immediately after clearing."

---
Current implementation status:
Steps existing in some form: 1, 2, 3 (partial — no 
heuristic defaults yet), 4, 5, 10, 11, 12 (partial — 
reminders only, not paste-ready packets), 14.
Steps missing: 6 (candidate↔JSON reconciliation), 
7 (ARIA state capture), 8 (DECISIONS/ANTI_PATTERNS/
INVARIANTS prompts), 9 (naming scan), 13 (session summary).
Each session adds one or two missing steps.

This is the target. Build toward it incrementally.

[2026-05-08] — Governance heat and core emotional value

🧠 Governance heat — ARIA should eventually monitor the 
governance-to-output ratio. Systems like this can become 
self-referential, process-addicted, ceremony-heavy. 
ARIA notices when too much overhead is accumulating 
relative to productive work and warns: "governance 
overhead rising — time to ship something."

🔭 Core emotional value proposition of ARIA — not 
"smarter AI" or "faster coding" or "automation" but:
"reduced continuity burden"
"you don't have to remember everything"
That's the deepest human value. Everything else is 
implementation detail.

🔭 The system now has differentiated continuity scopes:
- Lightweight continuity: clear
- Heavyweight continuity: handoff
- Ambient continuity: 🔭/🧠 markers during work
- Operational continuity: AMORTIZED GOVERNANCE RULE
- Governance continuity: LOCKED_ATTRIBUTES evolution
All without collapsing into one giant ritual.

[2026-05-08] — Handoff metrics / continuity observability

Not productivity metrics. Continuity integrity metrics.

Eventually ARIA should track:
- continuity integrity score
- unresolved branch count
- governance debt (stale candidates, unpromoted rules)
- unsynced ARIA ideas
- reconstruction confidence

"Continuity observability" — once the system becomes 
operationally real, you need to be able to see its 
health at a glance, not just feel it.

Future layer. Not now. Stabilize first.

## Trio Repo Symmetry (2026-05-09)

For the first time, all three trio roles can independently verify repo state:
- GPT: GitHub connected — direct read access
- Claude chat: GitHub Integration connected — direct read access  
- Code: local file access — always had full read

Cross-role reconciliation is now structurally possible without user acting as relay.
This changes handoff cost shape: Block B becomes lighter, Layer 2 restoration 
becomes a fetch instead of a paste, and AI-to-AI verification no longer depends 
on trusting each other's reports.

Preservation: ARIA_IDEAS
Classification: Architectural insight — trio coordination
